## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics (homogeneous reaction rate laws)
**Analysis**: The task involves predicting the rate of change of a species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of concentration (A) and time (t). This is the central differential equation in chemical kinetics, where the rate law typically depends on the current concentration(s) and possibly explicitly on time if the rate coefficient is time-dependent (e.g., catalyst deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 (constant reaction rate, e.g., surface saturation or photochemical reaction under constant light)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular reaction, exponential decay of reactant)
- Second-order decay (single reactant): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular dimerization or second-order consumption of a single species)
- Mixed-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (concurrent first- and second-order processes)
- Autocatalytic (logistic) rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction, sigmoidal concentration-time profile)
- Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate increases then decreases with A due to inhibitory binding)
- Reversible first-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (equilibrating reaction, net rate approaches zero at equilibrium)
- Time-dependent exponential decay of rate: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or radiation source decay causing rate constant to decrease)
- Power-law time-dependent rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A * t**c1 (non-isothermal or fractal-like kinetics, stretched exponential derivative)
- Prout–Tompkins model for autocatalytic reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (1 - A)**c2 (generalized nucleation and growth kinetics, often used in solid-state thermogravimetry)
- Sestak–Berggren model: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (1 - A)**c2 * (-log(1 - A))**c3 (flexible model for complex solid-state or polymer degradation kinetics)
- Avrami–Erofeev derivative form: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * exp(-c2 * t**c3) (nucleation and growth processes where rate depends explicitly on time)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 + c1 * (c2 - A) * (c3 - A) (equilibrium of dimerization or two-reactant reversible reaction)
- Hill-type cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative substrate binding with sigmoidal rate-concentration curve)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple order reactions: rate proportional to integer or fractional power of concentration → dA_dt ∝ A**c
- Autocatalysis: rate proportional to product of reactant and product concentrations, leading to bell-shaped or symmetric sigmoidal conversion curves → structure A*(c - A)
- Enzyme saturation: rate approaches a maximum velocity at high concentration, mathematically expressed by a rational function with linear denominator → A/(K + A)
- Substrate inhibition: rate first increases then decreases with concentration, requiring a higher-order (A²) term in the denominator → A/(K1 + A + K2 A²)
- Reversibility: rate includes both negative (forward) and positive (reverse) terms, often linear in concentration, leading to an offset equilibrium → -c0*A + c1
- Time-dependent rate coefficients (aging/deactivation): explicit time multiplication, often exponential or power-law, reflects loss of catalytic activity → exp(ct)*A or t**c * A
- Solid-state or gel kinetics: often follow the Prout–Tompkins or Sestak–Berggren models containing product terms of A, (1-A), and logarithmic terms
- Nucleation-and-growth: rate may have bell-shaped dependence on time with explicit t term independent of A, often originating from Avrami-type models → t**n exp(-kt**m)
- Diffusion-limited reactions: rate may show inverse square root of time dependence when coupled with concentration, e.g., dA_dt ∝ A/sqrt(t) inside a particle
- Cooperative binding in enzymatic or transport kinetics: rate exhibits sigmoidal dependence on concentration described by a Hill-type rational function with exponent > 1
